  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ef3338fa-6467-4b86-ac2b-b8c96e743985'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

Simon Illyan, head of ImpSec and Miles’ former boss, is failing physically and mentally, and Miles sets out to find out why -- and who, if anyone, is behind Illyan’s rapid decline. Library Journal calls Miles “one of the genre’s most enterprising and engaging heroes”. A Hugo and Nebula Award finalist.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_918863298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/918863298" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/918863298?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781433201141" href="/book/show/1141958.Memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=scifi-modern">scifi-modern</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=super-private-journal">super-private-journal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=x-vorkosigan-saga">x-vorkosigan-saga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer918863298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7896493823463121206">a colleague asked me a series of questions while we were out drinking the other night, questions like <i>So what's next for you?</i> and <i>Is this all you are planning on doing with your career?</i> and <i>Is your current job how you want to be defined and does that actually give you satisfaction?</i> I found myself annoyed then defensive then offended. what gave her the right to question me, I've accomplished a lot in my job and in my life, yes I am content with my career and why the hell shouldn't I be, blah blah</span>
  <span id="freeText7896493823463121206" style="display:none">a colleague asked me a series of questions while we were out drinking the other night, questions like <i>So what's next for you?</i> and <i>Is this all you are planning on doing with your career?</i> and <i>Is your current job how you want to be defined and does that actually give you satisfaction?</i> I found myself annoyed then defensive then offended. what gave her the right to question me, I've accomplished a lot in my job and in my life, yes I am content with my career and why the hell shouldn't I be, blah blah blah. in the end I realized that I shouldn't have been offended because I think she was asking me those questions because she was asking herself the same. and so I calmed down and we continued to get drunk while philosophizing on the choices we've made and the nature of our existence blah blah blah.<br /><br />I think some people like to live in boxes. I am such a person. I love my box, it's a safe and comfortable one and I've spent a lifetime constructing it. my box is one that gives me genuine satisfaction and the feeling that I am doing only what I want to be doing with my life. but I think other people resent and reject the idea of a box; they prefer to live in what can be called a "liminal space" - that space between, that place of ambiguity and movement and looking towards what comes next. you can look at your goals in life and try to come up with a plan or timeline to achieve those goals. or you can look at your goals and see them as constantly in flux, in movement depending on where you are, liminal. or you can look at yourself and realize that you are actually not a goal-oriented person. I think all of those are different kinds of boxes. I think my colleague may disagree.<br /><br />so this book, Memory, is about those sorts of things. despite opening with a character getting his legs shot off and ending with a high-stakes trap for a devious villain, this is far from an action novel. it is a thoughtful story about who we are, why we are, the boxes we construct, the identities we create for ourselves and the separate boxes those identities live in, how our identity/identities can become dominos or houses of cards falling if something or someone takes those boxes away. Miles Vorkosigan's dual identities of mercenary fleet commander and aristocratic peer of the realm have always been bubbling in the background throughout his stories; in this novel they finally come to a head. Bujold does a superb and moving job in delineating who Miles is, and was, and can be; she gives the mundane, all-too-common situations of making errors &amp; trying to cover up your tracks, losing a job &amp; so losing a part of your identity, a palpably emotional resonance. she does all of that and then she doubles down and gives us another ongoing character, Simon Illyan, going through a similar thing but in an entirely different manner. Miles is the sort of character who assertively rejects the idea of a box and who insists he lives in a liminal space - but who has actually been constructing two boxes to live in, and has actively <i>not</i> been living in the space between, in that liminal space. Simon is the sort of character who has constructed his own perfect box - one that makes his career equal his actual self - only to find that box dismantled and his sureness of purpose and self destroyed as he moves into a purely liminal space. it is fascinating comparing the two journeys.<br /><br />in sum, this is a wonderful novel about figuring out that <i>who you are</i> does not equal your job or your birth name or any specific, singular role or title; rather, it is the sum of all such things, and your experiences, and your internal workings, your actions and your potential, your ability to change or not change, and so much else. <i>you</i> = not easily summed up in one word.<br /><br />I love that this space opera is all about these 'mysteries' that every human experiences. I know when I pick up a Vorkosigan Saga novel that I will be enjoying some action and some intrigue and some political maneuvering and maybe even some romance. standard space opera pleasures. but I also know that I will be enjoying a human tale about actual human beings and the things that happen in life, to everyone. it is that last sentence, that particular quality, that makes this series so special.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7896493823463121206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1961761015" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1961761015" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1961761015?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1961761015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9575258963230937780"><b>A buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maria</a>.</b><br/><br/>I gave none of the books of the series 5 stars despite the fact that I like it a lot. The reason for this is that you can predict what would happen in the next book by the time you finish the previous one. So in the last book it turned out Miles began having unpredictable seizures. Anybody wants to bet where it goes in this novel? Right, his complete inability to lead his mercenary fleet. And thus Miles ended up grounded - a result of not one, but two big miscal</span>
  <span id="freeText9575258963230937780" style="display:none"><b>A buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova" rel="nofollow noopener">Maria</a>.</b><br><br>I gave none of the books of the series 5 stars despite the fact that I like it a lot. The reason for this is that you can predict what would happen in the next book by the time you finish the previous one. So in the last book it turned out Miles began having unpredictable seizures. Anybody wants to bet where it goes in this novel? Right, his complete inability to lead his mercenary fleet. And thus Miles ended up grounded - a result of not one, but two big miscalculations of his both originated with his medical condition mentioned above.<br><br>Miles was grounded in his home planet and his home estate currently populated by a security guard and a feral cat. After a lot of brooding (and I do mean - a lot) he recalled he was a High Lord and as such had some obligations towards his people. Trying to help a friend he stuck his nose where it did not belong and after a little time realized he might have bitten more than he could chew. People familiar with the character know that if he has a chance to speak he can and will talk his way out of practically any sticky situation no matter how life threatening it is. <br><br>As you can imagine from the above description the book is a big departure from the previous usual space opera genre with space ships shooting at each other and individual people doing the same and Miles emerging victorious. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491869693i/22456244._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="230" alt="Shooting" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This time it is more like a detective story - after our hero was done with his brooding which happened just before the middle of the book. Do not expect the grand mystery of the type which would keep Agatha Christie awake at night guessing the identity of the culprit as it is fairly obvious from the beginning and it does not give much credit to Miles that he did not see it right away. It - the mystery - serves its purpose though.<br><br>Miles developed as a character. In this context it means the series moved from action space opera into interplanetary politics territory. It is good? Time will tell. Sufficient to say that for now the rating is very firm 4 stars, although I thought about lowering it to 3. Can you guess the part which tempted me? Right, brooding part. Long brooding part. Very long brooding part. Extremely long brooding part. Extraordinary long brooding part. I hope you got the idea. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491869427i/22456203._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="210" alt="Brooding" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9575258963230937780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1874231560" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874231560" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874231560?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874231560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12432185989378870354"><b>*** 5 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with Evgeny and Maria because we love Science Fiction!!!</b><br/><br/>Wow! I always knew that this series is special, but books like this one, emotional and poignant, are what make this series AMAZING! <br/><br/>Miles Vorkosigan, at the beginning of the book as his alternate persona Miles Naismith, Admiral of the Dendarii Mercenaries, is in trouble. After being criogenically preserved and subsequently restored back to life, is suffering with seizures as a complication of his rushed defreezing. Kno</span>
  <span id="freeText12432185989378870354" style="display:none"><b>*** 5 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with Evgeny and Maria because we love Science Fiction!!!</b><br /><br />Wow! I always knew that this series is special, but books like this one, emotional and poignant, are what make this series AMAZING! <br /><br />Miles Vorkosigan, at the beginning of the book as his alternate persona Miles Naismith, Admiral of the Dendarii Mercenaries, is in trouble. After being criogenically preserved and subsequently restored back to life, is suffering with seizures as a complication of his rushed defreezing. Knowing that if his superiors find out they will ground him to planet, Miles is hiding his seizures, until one of those happens during a rescue mission and he almost kills the person he is supposed to be rescuing. He attempts to hide the truth in his report knowing nothing good could come of it, and is urgently called back to Barryarr. Quinn is mad with him, Elena and her husband seem to be saying goodbye, Wolf-girl is the only gentle, calming influence he has on his trip home, but even she goes her own way once they land. An empty house stuck in the past awaits him and he is terrified that another seizure could overwhelm him at any moment... Miles is already melancholy when faced with his boss Simon's questions and he chooses the wrong answer. At this moment the world he has created for himself crumbles around him and life as he knows it is changed irrevocably. <br /><br />I wanted to scream, to shake him and make him take all the bad choices back! I wanted to cry, having been a witness to one of the most heart-wrenching, embarrassing, world-changing moments for two people who obviously have a lot of love and respect for one another. Simon's deep disappointment, Miles' realization that he really, really scrued up and can't dig himself out of the pit he buried himself into, and the knowledge that either one would give anything to change it, but their honer would not let them, this was one of the most emotional and memorable scenes I have come across in a very long time. The strength of this moment and all together the series comes from the deceptively simple prose and straight forward approach to storytelling. I LOVE this author!!!<br /><br />From there on the story becomes one of people loosing the image of who they are, the loss of the things they build their self-identity around, the understanding of what makes them individuals... Miles and Simon are forced to say goodbye to the very constructs the rest of the world has come to know of them and try to survive the total defragmentation.... Neither man is ready to deal with it, but life doesn't pull its punches and while turning 30 years old, Miles has to not only survive, but find debts in himself he was not aware of being there... He is pushed through the hump of self-destruction by his friends, the people whose lives he had impacted, and his very useful connections with people in high places... What makes him go past existing and toward recreating himself from foundation up is the desire to find out who he really is and use that to refortify the circle of support he takes responsibility for. This is why his first step to rebuilding is to take care of Simon who is in trouble himself.... <br /><br />I loooooved Ivan here! He is such an unassuming dude, who has figured out early in life that if you play clueless, people tend to not pile up responsibilities on him, and playing dumb is even better. But he is a Vor and he is smart and reliable, so he has stopped being able to fool his cousin and aunty:-). Cordelia is one of the greatest female characters ever, so the only complaint I have there is not enough page time!!! Gregor shines as a very smart and capable leader, but I didn't feel comfortable with him poaching on another, despite it being what the girl wanted too. The mystery, which seemed like the skeletal structure on which the character development was propped up, was OK, but the star of the show was the complete breakdown and subsequent rebuilding of Miles and Simon. We got to say goodbye to many things, which broke my ❤, but the story left us with promises of things to come, and I am looking forward to reading every step of the way! <br /><br />Although this book was slower and more contemplative, it is just as intense and palpitations inducing as the others, only planet side and a tad melancholy. Hope you all give this series a chance ☺!<br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and may you always find what you need in the pages of a Good book!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12432185989378870354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655710?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="thefourthvine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="thefourthvine" href="/user/show/115625-thefourthvine">thefourthvine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671878450" href="/book/show/837220.Memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115625-thefourthvine?shelf=sff">sff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8757893151844748325">This is my favorite of all the Vorkosigan books (although, oh my god, don't start here; you have to read all the ones that came before it to appreciate it), because in it, Bujold does something very difficult very well: she massively changes the main character of an ongoing, established series.<br/><br/>Series tend to stagnate because authors don't let their characters develop in any but inconsequential ways. Bujold has never had that problem; Miles has grown up over the course of the books he's in, devel</span>
  <span id="freeText8757893151844748325" style="display:none">This is my favorite of all the Vorkosigan books (although, oh my god, don't start here; you have to read all the ones that came before it to appreciate it), because in it, Bujold does something very difficult very well: she massively changes the main character of an ongoing, established series.<br /><br />Series tend to stagnate because authors don't let their characters develop in any but inconsequential ways. Bujold has never had that problem; Miles has grown up over the course of the books he's in, developed, become a real adult. <br /><br />But it became obvious, in the novels preceding Memory, that Bujold had written herself into a corner: Miles couldn't develop anymore without major changes to his life and his character. And Bujold makes those changes, and <i>pulls it off</i>. <br /><br />I really don't want to spoil this here; if this is your thing, I want you to read it, see how she does it. So I will just say: wow. This is an impressive novel - fun plot, good pacing, strong narrative, and a character reboot done <i>right</i>. (And, to be honest, I wish I'd stopped reading the series here; this would've been the best ending note in all the world.)<br /></span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1010587095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2057722132960826515">This next novel is probably one of the most cogent and subtle of the stories, or at least it was probably one of the more profound. Loss took on a brand new spin this time. Loss of identity, purpose, and even his alternate life. Simon's tale was as interesting and heartwarming as it was also full of loss. How both of them got back on their feet was the main impetus of the story, although it was hardly a straight line. In Miles's case, it was part happy accident, a realization that he needed to m</span>
  <span id="freeText2057722132960826515" style="display:none">This next novel is probably one of the most cogent and subtle of the stories, or at least it was probably one of the more profound. Loss took on a brand new spin this time. Loss of identity, purpose, and even his alternate life. Simon's tale was as interesting and heartwarming as it was also full of loss. How both of them got back on their feet was the main impetus of the story, although it was hardly a straight line. In Miles's case, it was part happy accident, a realization that he needed to make up for his mistakes, and the need to do what was right. Fortunately, he could call in some major chips to speed him along the right path.<br /><br />It was an enheartening novel, and infinitely less flashy than some of the previous ones, but probably one of the most satisfying.</span>

<div id="review_349494055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349494055" />
    <a title="Clouds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds"><img alt="Clouds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514641128p2/9374686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349494055?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clouds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clouds" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds">Clouds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671016074" href="/book/show/1141957.Memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=pub-1990s">pub-1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=gifts">gifts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=vorkosigan-saga">vorkosigan-saga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349494055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17634328740798825039"><a href='http://www.theaceofclouds.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2' rel='nofollow noopener'>Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414?chapter=7' rel='nofollow noopener'>GIFTS AND GUILTY</a> list.<br/><br/>Regardless of how many books are already queued patiently on my reading list, unexpected gifts and guilt-trips will always see unplanned additions muscling their way in at the front.</b><br/><br/>A few weeks ago I came down quite suddenly with th</span>
  <span id="freeText17634328740798825039" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.theaceofclouds.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414?chapter=7" rel="nofollow noopener">GIFTS AND GUILTY</a> list.<br><br>Regardless of how many books are already queued patiently on my reading list, unexpected gifts and guilt-trips will always see unplanned additions muscling their way in at the front.</b><br><br>A few weeks ago I came down quite suddenly with the Norovirus which has swept across the UK this winter. One minute I was in bed complaining of a slight stomach ache, the next I was passing out on the bathroom floor after hurling into the sink, bath and finally toilet. My wife had some big exams coming up, so rather than nurse me she threw a bag and the baby into a taxi and went to stay with friends.<br><br>Because I couldn’t even keep water down, I quickly became dehydrated and my fever spiked. Have you ever had fever dreams? Weird aren’t they? I work for a finance company and had recently finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/147915.A_Storm_of_Swords" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Storm of Swords: Blood and Gold</i>
</a>. I was having very vivid dreams, trying to explain to Tyrion Lannister that I couldn’t approve his loan because he’d recently left his position as the King’s Hand, and we couldn’t lend to unemployed customers. I also had to turn down Daenerys Targaryen because she didn’t have three years residency in Westeros. <br><br>Once reality had reasserted itself (and my body would accept water again), I still needed a couple of days of quiet recovery. This book was a way down my reading list, but it was the one that found its way into my shaking hand and kept me company between my many naps. <br><br>If you’ve never read any of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40380-vorkosigan-saga" rel="nofollow noopener">Vorkosigan Saga</a>:<br>1) You lucky person, you have such a treat waiting for you – they’re great!<br>2) Don’t start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1141957.Memory" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>Memory</b>
  </i>
</a>.<br><br>This is very much a transition story. Up to this point Miles has been a quirky (but brilliant) space adventurer; a pintsize aristocrat officer working as an undercover intelligence agent, posing as a mercenary admiral. In this book – that all stops.<br><br>So if Miles is no longer Admiral Naismith, who is he? That’s the central question of this book. Everybody is moving on with their lives – Elena and Baz set the tone at the start when they tell Miles they’re retiring from the mercenary fleet to start a family, and then Emperor Gregor is falling in love too! Miles has been through so much, and what (aside from his wits) has he got to show for it?<br><br>The pace and intensity is lower here than some of the previous adventures. This is a lot more of a reflective, contemplative Miles that we’re used to. But he still needs an adventure, he can’t just brood – and the story here is predominantly a detective case, investigating who sabotaged the memory-chip in Simon Ilyan’s head (Miles ex-boss). But this slower pace is no bad thing – <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Bujold</a> is a character-centric writer, and taking her foot off the gas with the plot twists allows her time to dig deeper into the cast’s psyche – something she does very well indeed. <br><br>I often find that my state of mind plays a huge part in how much I enjoy a book. Recovering from the Norovirus could have been a very tiring and lonely time – but Miles Vorkosigan has joined that elite group of fictional characters who feel like old friends in my head. He was going through a tough time in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1141957.Memory" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>Memory</b>
  </i>
</a>, and I was doing likewise in Cardiff – it felt like we helped each other through it.<br><br>My admiration for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Bujold</a> grows with each and every book I read. I've got <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61884.Komarr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Komarr</i>
</a> lined up a few books down my reading list and I'm certainly looking forward to it!<br><br><b>After this I read: </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329873466" rel="nofollow noopener">Thomas</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17634328740798825039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9566041463367398464" style="display:none">Best. Miles. Yet.<br />I screwed up my sleep patterns for this book, and it was worth it. Just saying.<br /><br />I thought the last entry did some great character changes, with Miles injury and Mark's metamorphis. But here, Miles is in full-on identity crisis, and we also get to see Gregor making some life changes as well. I loved that, because Gregor is such a big part of their lives, but is not seen as much. So it was great to see him in such a happy place. Of course, their actions in moving on with their lives are going to create some other changes. Illyan, Ivan and Elli most notably.<br /><br />Bujold seems to handle this in stride, with new characters moving in, and the old moving not off, simply offstage. It creates great scope to this great story.</span>

<div id="review_1266130120" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1266130120" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1266130120?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10326608-lindsay?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1266130120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer954281019208894264">Part of a Vorkosigan reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2017/18. During my initial exposure to the Vorkosigan books, this one was actually the first of them that I'd read, and prior to reread I had not revisited it since then. As the novel that originally hooked me on the series even without all the backstory, I was really curious how it would hold up. I actually think it holds up very well indeed and actually forms a brilliant second volume of the soul-searching that began with the pr</span>
  <span id="freeText954281019208894264" style="display:none">Part of a Vorkosigan reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group in 2017/18. During my initial exposure to the Vorkosigan books, this one was actually the first of them that I'd read, and prior to reread I had not revisited it since then. As the novel that originally hooked me on the series even without all the backstory, I was really curious how it would hold up. I actually think it holds up very well indeed and actually forms a brilliant second volume of the soul-searching that began with the previous volume.<br /><br />The story starts with Miles back in action with the Dendarii Mercenaries. The relatively routine mission he's on goes disastrously wrong when he experiences a cryorevival-induced seizure mid-operation and causes a friendly fire incident. Fearing his Barrayaran ImpSec superiors will remove him from active operations, he falsifies the mission report. But of course ImpSec are very good at their jobs and he's found out. So his military career is over and almost for the first time since we met him in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61906.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice__Vorkosigan_Saga___2_" title="The Warrior's Apprentice (Vorkosigan Saga, #2) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior's Apprentice</a> we have Miles without Admiral Naismith.<br /><br />So who is Miles Vorkosigan <i>really</i>?<br /><br />The first half of the book is the wreckage of Miles trying to answer that question. But as usual with Miles, what he really needs is action, and he gets it in the form of an attack on Simon Illyan and an obdurate response from ImpSec in his recovery. This is a situation where Lord Vorkosigan is who's required rather than the little admiral.<br /><br />This book is an interesting one just from the point of view of a long series. It's distinctly the second part of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61909.Mirror_Dance__Vorkosigan_Saga___8_" title="Mirror Dance (Vorkosigan Saga, #8) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Mirror Dance</a>, it's also a pivotal story as Miles changes careers and perhaps for the first time becomes truly himself and recognized for his ability outside the tight confines of ImpSec security clearance. The first part is definitely slow, but it's also extremely necessary in the context of this nearly hyperactive who hasn't really stopped for a self-assessment since he graduated from the military academy.<br /><br />From the point of view of a reread, I remember this being the start of the golden run that is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory__Vorkosigan_Saga___10_" title="Memory (Vorkosigan Saga, #10) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Memory</a>-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61884.Komarr__Vorkosigan_Saga___11_" title="Komarr (Vorkosigan Saga, #11) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Komarr</a>-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61899.A_Civil_Campaign__Vorkosigan_Saga___12_" title="A Civil Campaign (Vorkosigan Saga, #12) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">A Civil Campaign</a>. Very much looking forward to next month's read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="954281019208894264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_364621721" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/364621721" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364621721?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=2020-reading-list">2020-reading-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=used-books">used-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=z-1990s">z-1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364621721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15930893441790994151">I always enjoy the adventures of Miles Vorkosigan, but this is the best book in the series so far in my opinion. I’ve always been entertained by Miles’ forward momentum, his dual roles as Lord Vorkosign and Admiral Naismith, and his willingness to plunge into danger with only a skeleton of plan. This is the book when Miles grows up and becomes a much better human being.<br/><br/>The book begins with Miles making a very serious error in judgement and being removed from his Imperial Security position by Sim</span>
  <span id="freeText15930893441790994151" style="display:none">I always enjoy the adventures of Miles Vorkosigan, but this is the best book in the series so far in my opinion. I’ve always been entertained by Miles’ forward momentum, his dual roles as Lord Vorkosign and Admiral Naismith, and his willingness to plunge into danger with only a skeleton of plan. This is the book when Miles grows up and becomes a much better human being.<br /><br />The book begins with Miles making a very serious error in judgement and being removed from his Imperial Security position by Simon Illyan, the head of ImpSec. Now, Lord Vorkosigan must find out who he is when he’s not pretending to be someone else. When something bad happens to Illyan, it is Miles who steps up to the plate and convinces the Emperor to let him investigate. This installment may not have interstellar travel or gun fights, it has a more “spy novel” vibe. <br /><br />I wonder if Bujold became tired of the military type adventures and decided to change Miles' life course? If so, I highly approve and I can hardly wait to read the next book in the series. <br /><br /><b>Book number 346 in my Science Fiction and Fantasy Reading Project.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15930893441790994151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_681286011" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681286011" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681286011?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781433201141" href="/book/show/1141958.Memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1audio">1audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681286011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11041661710563548263">This is well matched with the previous book chronologically. The last one explored Mark's psychology & life, this one deals with Miles. I liked it a lot better. Mark's had a lot of repetition, concentrated mostly on the few items we already knew of his past & his reactions to them over & over. While there wasn't any new information on Miles, he's a much better documented & a much more complex character. He very believably gets himself into & out of the trick bag on a regular basis, the main fun </span>
  <span id="freeText11041661710563548263" style="display:none">This is well matched with the previous book chronologically. The last one explored Mark's psychology &amp; life, this one deals with Miles. I liked it a lot better. Mark's had a lot of repetition, concentrated mostly on the few items we already knew of his past &amp; his reactions to them over &amp; over. While there wasn't any new information on Miles, he's a much better documented &amp; a much more complex character. He very believably gets himself into &amp; out of the trick bag on a regular basis, the main fun of this series. In this story, it's even better done than normal, though.<br /><br />Bujold has done a great job of setting up the situation &amp; does even better with the solution. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The Imperial Auditor position is new to the series, well introduced by the description of the old one while our attention is mostly on Miles meeting his victim. Even on my first read, I remember thinking this would be a perfect position for him, so when it is offered,  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> it seemed a natural growth rather than pasted on.<br /><br />She also allows the characters to grow, change, &amp; generally move through life. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ It's been obvious for some time that Admiral Naismith &amp; Lord Vorkosigan can't coexist forever. Cordelia's worries about what would happen to Miles when he had to choose (She says 'give up the little Admiral', but that could be wishful thinking.) &amp; his affair with Quinn have made this point for 2 or 3 books now.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Their decisions are often hard ones &amp; some are just a shame, but that just lends them more reality.<br /><br />All in all, I'm very pleased with both the book &amp; the series. No matter how you count it, there have been about 10 books so far. Most series go stale for me long before now. This one is like a soap opera, dragging me along to see what happens, then adds some new wrinkle that I want to see to the end. As usual, it was very well read. I'm on to the next one, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61884.Komarr__Vorkosigan_Saga___11_" title="Komarr (Vorkosigan Saga, #11) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Komarr</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11041661710563548263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18656418-justine?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2807219832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2468359465080821224">A very subtle and interesting book. Miles wrestles with his memory issues, which continue to vex although not cripple him. Much more complex memory issues do cripple his friend, who he then tries to assist by helping find the culprit who triggered the causal event. <br/><br/>While his friend struggles to rebuild himself and rediscover his identity, Miles undergoes a similar process. He has to attempt the difficult transformation from his invented identity, Admiral Miles Naismith, back to the person he has</span>
  <span id="freeText2468359465080821224" style="display:none">A very subtle and interesting book. Miles wrestles with his memory issues, which continue to vex although not cripple him. Much more complex memory issues do cripple his friend, who he then tries to assist by helping find the culprit who triggered the causal event. <br /><br />While his friend struggles to rebuild himself and rediscover his identity, Miles undergoes a similar process. He has to attempt the difficult transformation from his invented identity, Admiral Miles Naismith, back to the person he has always run away from, Lord Miles Vorkosigan.<br /><br />I liked the parallel in the examination of identity between the two characters, and the way Miles draws strength from helping to resolve the situation of his friend. There are many excellent scenes, but the one in particular I loved was where Miles is offered a temptation almost beyond refusal. The writing in this scene is incredibly vivid in its descriptions, capturing all the conflicting and uncontrolled feelings and sensations one would expect in this situation. <br /><br />An excellent transition story that not only resituates Miles in the next part of his overall story arc, but transforms him in a necessary way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2468359465080821224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9593244596002823440" style="display:none">Well, Miles has put his foot in it good this time...whatever shall he do????? Why come up smelling like, well if not like roses at least not like that solid waste stuff that's always hitting the rotary impeller whenever he gets involved.<br /><br />If you've followed Miles from early on in his "life" and like me have enjoyed his adventures then you won't be let down here. While early on I found these books occasionally hitting "speed bumps" where the story slowed down over time and installments of the saga that were better than others. While these aren't always exactly action filled speed rides they are enthralling reads.<br /><br />Here we're moving into a new facet of Miles life and carrier. We see further development in not only the over all story and plot(s) but in the characters themselves. Lives change in this one and we get not only a new adventure but the setup for and beginning what will follow.<br /><br />This is a good book, a satisfying addition to an excellent science fiction series. </span>

<div id="review_3460988651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3460988651" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10818276-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341872613p2/10818276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3460988651?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/10818276-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29765919-memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=american-authors">american-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=netgalleyreaders2020">netgalleyreaders2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=set-in-space">set-in-space</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=vorkosigan-series-challenge">vorkosigan-series-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3460988651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13661520423962614491">At a risk of repeating myself, this is my favourite Miles book thus far.<br/><br/>I have discovered that, despite preferring space opera over the other subgenres of scifi, I rather the Vorkosigan books full of political intrigue and set on Barrayar than the action adventure/space setting installments. I also prefer Lord Vorkosigan over Admiral Naismith, and Memory is truly the first book that focuses on the Vor Lord instead of the admiral for quite a while.<br/>The opening chapters show the medical side effect</span>
  <span id="freeText13661520423962614491" style="display:none">At a risk of repeating myself, this is my favourite Miles book thus far.<br /><br />I have discovered that, despite preferring space opera over the other subgenres of scifi, I rather the Vorkosigan books full of political intrigue and set on Barrayar than the action adventure/space setting installments. I also prefer Lord Vorkosigan over Admiral Naismith, and Memory is truly the first book that focuses on the Vor Lord instead of the admiral for quite a while.<br />The opening chapters show the medical side effects and debilitating seizures Miles has been enduring following his ‘death’. His ill health, and his concealment of it, forces Miles to yield his command of the Dendarii fleet and return to Barrayar.<br /><br />Soon after Miles's arrival planetside, his Impsec boss, Simon Illyan, has a memory chip (which was implanted in his brain years ago) go haywire. Illyan’s mental and physical health declines at such a rapid rate that he needs to resign his commission, leaving Miles without any chance of reinstatement when Illyan’s successor does not appreciate Miles’s... unique qualities. Miles does not, of course, let that stop him and the book's mystery plot is that of Miles investigating whether or not Illyan’s chip was sabotaged deliberately.<br /><br />Although I always enjoy Miles solving a mystery, I found a lot of this book incredibly sad. Both Illyan and Miles have to discover what type of men they will be without their military personas. Somehow LMB makes all this introspective reflection and searching for identity far from boring. As LMB showed in Mirror Dance, Illyan and Miles have a lovely pseudo father/son relationship, and she raised the poignancy level in Memory again by showing us the respect and love they share. *sniff* I also loved how the situation evoked memories for Miles of his grandfather. *sniff*<br />It’s not just the Miles and Illyan show, my other favs Ivan, Gregor, Galeni and Taura get some quality scenes and we even get a couple featuring Cordelia and Aral (happy sigh).<br /><br />Amongst the tears, LMB includes her trademark humour, a lot coming from a hilarious new character, Miles’s stand in driver-cum-butler Martin. Ivan is, of course, still the brunt of several jokes and I pretty much laughed out loud at Miles offering him a cat and his reaction to one of the romantic subplots (might I just add, this romance was the cutest!). <br /><br />Memory was another of the longer books in the series but again, like Mirror Dance, I flew through it, probably ignoring real life far too much to find out Miles’s fate (for now). And of course I'm now sucked in to starting Komarr immediately.<br /><br />5 out of 5 obviously</span>
  <a data-text-id="13661520423962614491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_886367921" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/886367921" />
    <a title="Stuart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart"><img alt="Stuart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452041473p2/9456990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/886367921?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart">Stuart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781433201141" href="/book/show/1141958.Memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=humanistic-sf">humanistic-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=military-sf">military-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer886367921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer30089456538742567"><b>Memory: An Identity Crisis for Miles - Which is the Real One?</b><br/><b>Memory</b> is the 8th volume in the Miles Vorkosigan Saga (if you exclude the stand-alones <b>Ethan of Athos</b> and <b>Falling Free</b>), and represents an important transitional phase between his free-wheeling alter-ego as Admiral Miles Naismith of the Dendarii Mercenaries, and Lord Miles Vorkosigan, son of Count Aral Vorkosigan and a key member of Emperor Gregor's inner circle of Barrayaran leaders. Therefore, this is definitely the wrong place to st</span>
  <span id="freeText30089456538742567" style="display:none"><b>Memory: An Identity Crisis for Miles - Which is the Real One?</b><br /><b>Memory</b> is the 8th volume in the Miles Vorkosigan Saga (if you exclude the stand-alones <b>Ethan of Athos</b> and <b>Falling Free</b>), and represents an important transitional phase between his free-wheeling alter-ego as Admiral Miles Naismith of the Dendarii Mercenaries, and Lord Miles Vorkosigan, son of Count Aral Vorkosigan and a key member of Emperor Gregor's inner circle of Barrayaran leaders. Therefore, this is definitely the wrong place to start reading the series - you'll not understand any of the background or experiences of Miles that have led up to this point. Therefore, of all the Miles Vorkosigan books, I felt this one was the least self-contained in the series, but a crucial transition point for Miles' character as he hits middle age and a sudden fork in his career and life path.<br /><br />The story opens with an action-packed rescue mission by the Dendarii mercenaries led by Miles, but quickly goes disastrously wrong. As a result of this debacle and Miles' attempt to cover it up to ImpSec and Simon Illyan, he suddenly finds himself cut off from both the Dendarii and the Barryaran military, and in a mid-life crisis as he two key identities, which are so well developed they have taken on a life of their own. So what happens to a person when both are snatched away without warning?<br /><br />Miles returns to House Vorkosigan, now empty of everything but memories, and tries to readjust to the stifling role of as a Vor lordling, but without the outlet of his Admiral Naismith identity or his pride as a military officer, the trapping of aristocracy are little solace. He visits the setting of the story "Mountains of Mourning", and does a lot of introspection and reflection on who he really is, and what gives his life purpose. This is another reason not to start with this book - it would be like starting the third season of a long-running drama.<br /><br />Of course just ruminations and mid-life crisis do not a SF adventure make, so Miles does soon encounter some very eccentric behavior by long-time ImpSec chief Simon Illyan, and as these start to escalate he realizes something very sinister is happening inside the organization, and when he himself if framed for it, he needs to go back into Miles Vorkosigan hyperactive mind mode and use his wits to exonerate himself and track down the real culprit. So the book's pace and mystery are more like <b>Cetaganda</b> than the space opera military adventures of the earlier books.<br /><br />It's a natural progression for Miles to start to grow out of his swash-buckling mercenary 20s, and as Mrs. Bujold has devoted so much care into fleshing out all the characters in this series, this book can devote itself to the inner struggle of Miles to come to grips with the inevitable life changes he and some of his close companions must go through, just like any of us. And she handles the story very well, as his inner monologues and thoughts are entirely realistic and consistent with all he has gone through before. <b>Memory</b> also sets the stage for a new phase of Miles' life, and it takes great confidence for an author to take a successful series and refuse to repeat the same formula over and over again, but instead force the main character to make changes he would rather not undergo, and still keep readers engaged in his story. Along with <b>Mirror Dance</b>, it's one of the most thoughtful and introspective of the Miles stories, and thought it may not be as exciting as earlier stories, it is done very well indeed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="30089456538742567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_492471508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/492471508" />

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/12621704-memory">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=barrayar">barrayar</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492471508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11241954124178727919"><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evgeny</a>.</b><br/><br/>WARNING SPOILERS AHEAD! <br/><br/>It's time to turn a new page in the Vorkosigan Saga and <i>Memory</i> is the transition point. When you read the books in the chronological order the reader can predict the initial events in the book with ease. It's a painful way to give Miles a much needed kick in the behind. Miles had reached the top as Admiral Neismith and sometimes I think that deep down inside he was no longer satisfied with that life. Why else would he sabotage himself so b</span>
  <span id="freeText11241954124178727919" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>.</b><br /><br />WARNING SPOILERS AHEAD! <br /><br />It's time to turn a new page in the Vorkosigan Saga and <i>Memory</i> is the transition point. When you read the books in the chronological order the reader can predict the initial events in the book with ease. It's a painful way to give Miles a much needed kick in the behind. Miles had reached the top as Admiral Neismith and sometimes I think that deep down inside he was no longer satisfied with that life. Why else would he sabotage himself so badly? Especially since he knows how good Simon's network of spies really is. Yes, it was painful to watch and even though I've read the book many times I still wanted to smack Miles on the head and save him the pain.<br /><br /><i>Memory</i> is a book about moving on, forgiving yourself, accepting that not all screw-ups can be swept under the rug and that you won't always be able to turn defeat into victory. It's also about friendship and loyalty, about honor and reputation - a recurring theme in the series one that will be explored yet again very soon. And now it's time to let Lord Vorkosigan shine and to move to my favourite part of the series - Miles's adventures as a Lord Auditor :D<br /><br />This is my favourite book in the series, not because of some outstanding writing or originality plot-wise but because more than a decade ago I picked up this book at a secondhand books stand while mindlessly browsing the boxes filled with books. I had no idea it's part of a series, thanks to the ridiculous way it's published in my country, but I thought it looked interesting. Little did I know that I've just picked a book from what would eventually become my very favourite series, one I reach for when I'm feeling particularly down or when I can't get out of a reading slump. Back then my English was awful, I had no idea ebooks existed and most of the books were publish before I could even read! As a result finding the rest of the series was one hell of a challenge and even now there's still some books I don't own a physical copy of. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11241954124178727919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer380136135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer430978803936584472">This highly satisfying read represents a fine apex point in a space opera series. It can be read alone as it represents a synthesis and resolution of the risky strategy taken in prior volumes by its protagonist Miles Vorkosigan in forging an alternative life to surmount his physical handicaps and restricted choices in the ruling class of a hereditary aristocracy. Miles in his youth finds a way to thrive as the leader of a mercenary fleet tasked with undercover operations for the Imperial space n</span>
  <span id="freeText430978803936584472" style="display:none">This highly satisfying read represents a fine apex point in a space opera series. It can be read alone as it represents a synthesis and resolution of the risky strategy taken in prior volumes by its protagonist Miles Vorkosigan in forging an alternative life to surmount his physical handicaps and restricted choices in the ruling class of a hereditary aristocracy. Miles in his youth finds a way to thrive as the leader of a mercenary fleet tasked with undercover operations for the Imperial space navy and excels in diverse adventures in a galaxy of several competitive human empires connected by wormholes. In this tale, his epilepsy after his recovery from severe injuries and battlefield cryopreservation forces him to return home. His depression over leaving his undercover life behind is turned around when he becomes engaged by a crisis surrounding a sudden medical problem of the Imperial intelligence director. The action is thrilling and fun without resorting to shoot-em-ups one might expect from this genre, and the development of Miles' character and that of others that richly populate this tale are successful in both emotional engagement and humor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="430978803936584472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17348327579918820599">I have dearly loved all of the Miles books, for a number of reasons. This one ranks as my favorite. Why? I laughed, snickered and guffawed out loud more times than I can remember, and was genuinely moved by Miles' decision to lay his Peter Pan existence aside, in order to grow up.   <span id="freeText17348327579918820599" style="display:none">I have dearly loved all of the Miles books, for a number of reasons. This one ranks as my favorite. Why? I laughed, snickered and guffawed out loud more times than I can remember, and was genuinely moved by Miles' decision to lay his Peter Pan existence aside, in order to grow up. I have gone through a similar experience these past months, perhaps that is why the book resonates so deeply with me. For both Miles and myself, the change was unexpected, and our lives are moving in a direction that could not have been predicted, but we're moving forward. And I'm, like Miles, not at all unhappy about it. But whatever the reason, this chapter in the Vorkosigan saga is my most treasured. </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2135825-trike?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3580450958920723623">This is a tremendous entry in Miles Vorkosigan adventures. For the first third not much happens and I was enthralled. Then the plot truly kicks in and I was riveted. This has all the stuff that makes these books so great: snark, heartfelt emotion, Jeeves & Wooster banter between Miles and Ivan, characters growing and changing, kittens.... It’s just pure feel-good sci-fi.<br/><br/>This is officially the tenth book in the Vorkosigan series and coincidentally the tenth Vorkosigan book I’ve listened to this y</span>
  <span id="freeText3580450958920723623" style="display:none">This is a tremendous entry in Miles Vorkosigan adventures. For the first third not much happens and I was enthralled. Then the plot truly kicks in and I was riveted. This has all the stuff that makes these books so great: snark, heartfelt emotion, Jeeves &amp; Wooster banter between Miles and Ivan, characters growing and changing, kittens.... It’s just pure feel-good sci-fi.<br /><br />This is officially the tenth book in the Vorkosigan series and coincidentally the tenth Vorkosigan book I’ve listened to this year. (My 11th overall.) That sort of coincidence with this book continued, as I happened to listen to the episode “Loops” of the Radiolab podcast this week (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wnycstudios.org/story/radiolab-loops">https://www.wnycstudios.org/story/rad...</a>), which featured a story about a woman who suffered from temporary global amnesia, which meant she couldn’t form new memories for about a day. It’s captured in this YouTube video: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/N3fA5uzWDU8">https://youtu.be/N3fA5uzWDU8</a> This exact thing happens to Miles’ boss at ImpSec, Simon Illyan, which was a cool, if strange parallel.<br /><br />That’s when the mystery kicks in, and all the necessary bits are already in place by the time that happens, allowing the story to barrel along to its satisfactory conclusion. Bujold is really hitting on all cylinders here, and I enjoyed every minute of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3580450958920723623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
